158 /// Utility function for reservePreviousStackSlotForValue. Tries to find ----
159 /// stack slot index to which we have spilled value for previous statepoints. ----
160 /// LookUpDepth specifies maximum DFS depth this function is allowed to look. ----
161 static std::optional findPreviousSpillSlot(const Value *Val, 0
162 SelectionDAGBuilder &Builder, ----
163 int LookUpDepth) { ----
164 // Can not look any further - give up now ----
165 if (LookUpDepth <= 0) 0
166 return std::nullopt; 0
167 ----
168 // Spill location is known for gc relocates ----
169 if (const auto *Relocate = dyn_cast(Val)) { 0
170 const Value *Statepoint = Relocate->getStatepoint(); 0
171 assert((isa(Statepoint) || isa(Statepoint)) && 0
172 "GetStatepoint must return one of two types"); ----
173 if (isa(Statepoint)) 0
174 return std::nullopt; 0
175 ----
176 const auto &RelocationMap = Builder.FuncInfo.StatepointRelocationMaps 0
177 [cast(Statepoint)]; 0
178 ----
179 auto It = RelocationMap.find(Relocate); 0
180 if (It == RelocationMap.end()) 0
181 return std::nullopt; 0
182 ----
183 auto &Record = It->second; 0
184 if (Record.type != RecordType::Spill) 0
185 return std::nullopt; 0
186 ----
187 return Record.payload.FI; 0
188 } ----
189 ----
190 // Look through bitcast instructions. ----
191 if (const BitCastInst *Cast = dyn_cast(Val)) 0
192 return findPreviousSpillSlot(Cast->getOperand(0), Builder, LookUpDepth - 1); 0
193 ----
194 // Look through phi nodes ----
195 // All incoming values should have same known stack slot, otherwise result ----
196 // is unknown. ----
197 if (const PHINode *Phi = dyn_cast(Val)) { 0
198 std::optional MergedResult; 0
199 ----
200 for (const auto &IncomingValue : Phi->incoming_values()) { 0
201 std::optional SpillSlot = ----
202 findPreviousSpillSlot(IncomingValue, Builder, LookUpDepth - 1); 0
203 if (!SpillSlot) 0
204 return std::nullopt; 0
205 ----
206 if (MergedResult && *MergedResult != *SpillSlot) 0
207 return std::nullopt; 0
208 ----
209 MergedResult = SpillSlot; 0
210 } ----
211 return MergedResult; 0
212 } ----
213 ----
214 // TODO: We can do better for PHI nodes. In cases like this: ----
215 // ptr = phi(relocated_pointer, not_relocated_pointer) ----
216 // statepoint(ptr) ----
217 // We will return that stack slot for ptr is unknown. And later we might ----
218 // assign different stack slots for ptr and relocated_pointer. This limits ----
219 // llvm's ability to remove redundant stores. ----
220 // Unfortunately it's hard to accomplish in current infrastructure. ----
221 // We use this function to eliminate spill store completely, while ----
222 // in example we still need to emit store, but instead of any location ----
223 // we need to use special "preferred" location. ----
224 ----
225 // TODO: handle simple updates. If a value is modified and the original ----
226 // value is no longer live, it would be nice to put the modified value in the ----
227 // same slot. This allows folding of the memory accesses for some ----
228 // instructions types (like an increment). ----
229 // statepoint (i) ----
230 // i1 = i+1 ----
231 // statepoint (i1) ----
232 // However we need to be careful for cases like this: ----
233 // statepoint(i) ----
234 // i1 = i+1 ----
235 // statepoint(i, i1) ----
236 // Here we want to reserve spill slot for 'i', but not for 'i+1'. If we just ----
237 // put handling of simple modifications in this function like it's done ----
238 // for bitcasts we might end up reserving i's slot for 'i+1' because order in ----
239 // which we visit values is unspecified. ----
240 ----
241 // Don't know any information about this instruction ----
242 return std::nullopt; 0
243 } ----

245 /// Return true if-and-only-if the given SDValue can be lowered as either a ----
246 /// constant argument or a stack reference. The key point is that the value ----
247 /// doesn't need to be spilled or tracked as a vreg use. ----
248 static bool willLowerDirectly(SDValue Incoming) { 0
249 // We are making an unchecked assumption that the frame size <= 2^16 as that ----
250 // is the largest offset which can be encoded in the stackmap format. ----
251 if (isa(Incoming)) 0
252 return true; 0
253 ----
254 // The largest constant describeable in the StackMap format is 64 bits. ----
255 // Potential Optimization: Constants values are sign extended by consumer, ----
256 // and thus there are many constants of static type > 64 bits whose value ----
257 // happens to be sext(Con64) and could thus be lowered directly. ----
258 if (Incoming.getValueType().getSizeInBits() > 64) 0
259 return false; 0
260 ----
261 return isIntOrFPConstant(Incoming) || Incoming.isUndef(); 0
262 } ----
263 ----
264 /// Try to find existing copies of the incoming values in stack slots used for ----
265 /// statepoint spilling. If we can find a spill slot for the incoming value, ----
266 /// mark that slot as allocated, and reuse the same slot for this safepoint. ----
267 /// This helps to avoid series of loads and stores that only serve to reshuffle ----
268 /// values on the stack between calls. ----
269 static void reservePreviousStackSlotForValue(const Value *IncomingValue, 0
270 SelectionDAGBuilder &Builder) { ----
271 SDValue Incoming = Builder.getValue(IncomingValue); 0
272 ----
273 // If we won't spill this, we don't need to check for previously allocated ----
274 // stack slots. ----
275 if (willLowerDirectly(Incoming)) 0
276 return; 0
277 ----
278 SDValue OldLocation = Builder.StatepointLowering.getLocation(Incoming); 0
279 if (OldLocation.getNode()) 0
280 // Duplicates in input ----
281 return; 0
282 ----
283 const int LookUpDepth = 6; 0
284 std::optional Index = ----
285 findPreviousSpillSlot(IncomingValue, Builder, LookUpDepth); 0
286 if (!Index) 0
287 return; 0
288 ----
289 const auto &StatepointSlots = Builder.FuncInfo.StatepointStackSlots; 0
290 ----
291 auto SlotIt = find(StatepointSlots, *Index); 0
292 assert(SlotIt != StatepointSlots.end() && 0
293 "Value spilled to the unknown stack slot"); ----
294 ----
295 // This is one of our dedicated lowering slots ----
296 const int Offset = std::distance(StatepointSlots.begin(), SlotIt); 0
297 if (Builder.StatepointLowering.isStackSlotAllocated(Offset)) { 0
298 // stack slot already assigned to someone else, can't use it! ----
299 // TODO: currently we reserve space for gc arguments after doing ----
300 // normal allocation for deopt arguments. We should reserve for ----
301 // _all_ deopt and gc arguments, then start allocating. This ----
302 // will prevent some moves being inserted when vm state changes, ----
303 // but gc state doesn't between two calls. ----
304 return; 0
305 } ----
306 // Reserve this stack slot ----
307 Builder.StatepointLowering.reserveStackSlot(Offset); 0
308 ----
309 // Cache this slot so we find it when going through the normal ----
310 // assignment loop. ----
311 SDValue Loc = ----
312 Builder.DAG.getTargetFrameIndex(*Index, Builder.getFrameIndexTy()); 0
313 Builder.StatepointLowering.setLocation(Incoming, Loc); 0
314 } ----

316 /// Extract call from statepoint, lower it and return pointer to the ----
317 /// call node. Also update NodeMap so that getValue(statepoint) will ----
318 /// reference lowered call result ----
319 static std::pair lowerCallFromStatepointLoweringInfo( 0
320 SelectionDAGBuilder::StatepointLoweringInfo &SI, ----
321 SelectionDAGBuilder &Builder) { ----
322 SDValue ReturnValue, CallEndVal; 0
323 std::tie(ReturnValue, CallEndVal) = 0
324 Builder.lowerInvokable(SI.CLI, SI.EHPadBB); 0
325 SDNode *CallEnd = CallEndVal.getNode(); 0
326 ----
327 // Get a call instruction from the call sequence chain. Tail calls are not ----
328 // allowed. The following code is essentially reverse engineering X86's ----
329 // LowerCallTo. ----
330 // ----
331 // We are expecting DAG to have the following form: ----
332 // ----
333 // ch = eh_label (only in case of invoke statepoint) ----
334 // ch, glue = callseq_start ch ----
335 // ch, glue = X86::Call ch, glue ----
336 // ch, glue = callseq_end ch, glue ----
337 // get_return_value ch, glue ----
338 // ----
339 // get_return_value can either be a sequence of CopyFromReg instructions ----
340 // to grab the return value from the return register(s), or it can be a LOAD ----
341 // to load a value returned by reference via a stack slot. ----
342 ----
343 bool HasDef = !SI.CLI.RetTy->isVoidTy(); 0
344 if (HasDef) { 0
345 if (CallEnd->getOpcode() == ISD::LOAD) 0
346 CallEnd = CallEnd->getOperand(0).getNode(); 0
347 else ----
348 while (CallEnd->getOpcode() == ISD::CopyFromReg) 0
349 CallEnd = CallEnd->getOperand(0).getNode(); 0
350 } ----
351 ----
352 assert(CallEnd->getOpcode() == ISD::CALLSEQ_END && "expected!"); 0
353 return std::make_pair(ReturnValue, CallEnd->getOperand(0).getNode()); 0
354 } ----

361 auto &MFI = MF.getFrameInfo(); 0

367 /// Spill a value incoming to the statepoint. It might be either part of ----
368 /// vmstate ----
369 /// or gcstate. In both cases unconditionally spill it on the stack unless it ----
370 /// is a null constant. Return pair with first element being frame index ----
371 /// containing saved value and second element with outgoing chain from the ----
372 /// emitted store ----
373 static std::tuple ----
374 spillIncomingStatepointValue(SDValue Incoming, SDValue Chain, 0
375 SelectionDAGBuilder &Builder) { ----
376 SDValue Loc = Builder.StatepointLowering.getLocation(Incoming); 0
377 MachineMemOperand* MMO = nullptr; 0
378 ----
379 // Emit new store if we didn't do it for this ptr before ----
380 if (!Loc.getNode()) { 0
381 Loc = Builder.StatepointLowering.allocateStackSlot(Incoming.getValueType(), 0
382 Builder); ----
383 int Index = cast(Loc)->getIndex(); 0
384 // We use TargetFrameIndex so that isel will not select it into LEA ----
385 Loc = Builder.DAG.getTargetFrameIndex(Index, Builder.getFrameIndexTy()); 0
386 ----
387 // Right now we always allocate spill slots that are of the same ----
388 // size as the value we're about to spill (the size of spillee can ----
389 // vary since we spill vectors of pointers too). At some point we ----
390 // can consider allowing spills of smaller values to larger slots ----
391 // (i.e. change the '==' in the assert below to a '>='). ----
392 MachineFrameInfo &MFI = Builder.DAG.getMachineFunction().getFrameInfo(); 0
393 assert((MFI.getObjectSize(Index) * 8) == 0
394 (-8 & (7 + // Round up modulo 8. ----
395 (int64_t)Incoming.getValueSizeInBits())) && ----
396 "Bad spill: stack slot does not match!"); ----
397 ----
398 // Note: Using the alignment of the spill slot (rather than the abi or ----
399 // preferred alignment) is required for correctness when dealing with spill ----
400 // slots with preferred alignments larger than frame alignment.. ----
401 auto &MF = Builder.DAG.getMachineFunction(); 0
402 auto PtrInfo = MachinePointerInfo::getFixedStack(MF, Index); 0
403 auto *StoreMMO = MF.getMachineMemOperand( 0
404 PtrInfo, MachineMemOperand::MOStore, MFI.getObjectSize(Index), 0
405 MFI.getObjectAlign(Index)); ----
406 Chain = Builder.DAG.getStore(Chain, Builder.getCurSDLoc(), Incoming, Loc, 0
407 StoreMMO); ----
408 ----
409 MMO = getMachineMemOperand(MF, *cast(Loc)); 0
410 ----
411 Builder.StatepointLowering.setLocation(Incoming, Loc); 0
412 } ----
413 ----
414 assert(Loc.getNode()); 0
415 return std::make_tuple(Loc, Chain, MMO); 0
416 } ----

418 /// Lower a single value incoming to a statepoint node. This value can be ----
419 /// either a deopt value or a gc value, the handling is the same. We special ----
420 /// case constants and allocas, then fall back to spilling if required. ----
421 static void ----
422 lowerIncomingStatepointValue(SDValue Incoming, bool RequireSpillSlot, 0
423 SmallVectorImpl &Ops, ----
424 SmallVectorImpl &MemRefs, ----
425 SelectionDAGBuilder &Builder) { ----
426 ----
427 if (willLowerDirectly(Incoming)) { 0
428 if (FrameIndexSDNode *FI = dyn_cast(Incoming)) { 0
429 // This handles allocas as arguments to the statepoint (this is only ----
430 // really meaningful for a deopt value. For GC, we'd be trying to ----
431 // relocate the address of the alloca itself?) ----
432 assert(Incoming.getValueType() == Builder.getFrameIndexTy() && 0
433 "Incoming value is a frame index!"); ----
434 Ops.push_back(Builder.DAG.getTargetFrameIndex(FI->getIndex(), 0
435 Builder.getFrameIndexTy())); ----
436 ----
437 auto &MF = Builder.DAG.getMachineFunction(); 0
438 auto *MMO = getMachineMemOperand(MF, *FI); 0
439 MemRefs.push_back(MMO); 0
440 return; 0
441 } ----
442 ----
443 assert(Incoming.getValueType().getSizeInBits() <= 64); 0
444 ----
445 if (Incoming.isUndef()) { 0
446 // Put an easily recognized constant that's unlikely to be a valid ----
447 // value so that uses of undef by the consumer of the stackmap is ----
448 // easily recognized. This is legal since the compiler is always ----
449 // allowed to chose an arbitrary value for undef. ----
450 pushStackMapConstant(Ops, Builder, 0xFEFEFEFE); 0
451 return; 0
452 } ----
453 ----
454 // If the original value was a constant, make sure it gets recorded as ----
455 // such in the stackmap. This is required so that the consumer can ----
456 // parse any internal format to the deopt state. It also handles null ----
457 // pointers and other constant pointers in GC states. ----
458 if (ConstantSDNode *C = dyn_cast(Incoming)) { 0
459 pushStackMapConstant(Ops, Builder, C->getSExtValue()); 0
460 return; 0
461 } else if (ConstantFPSDNode *C = dyn_cast(Incoming)) { 0
462 pushStackMapConstant(Ops, Builder, 0
463 C->getValueAPF().bitcastToAPInt().getZExtValue()); 0
464 return; 0
465 } ----
466 ----
467 llvm_unreachable("unhandled direct lowering case"); 0
468 } ----
469 ----
470 ----
471 ----
472 if (!RequireSpillSlot) { 0
473 // If this value is live in (not live-on-return, or live-through), we can ----
474 // treat it the same way patchpoint treats it's "live in" values. We'll ----
475 // end up folding some of these into stack references, but they'll be ----
476 // handled by the register allocator. Note that we do not have the notion ----
477 // of a late use so these values might be placed in registers which are ----
478 // clobbered by the call. This is fine for live-in. For live-through ----
479 // fix-up pass should be executed to force spilling of such registers. ----
480 Ops.push_back(Incoming); 0
481 } else { ----
482 // Otherwise, locate a spill slot and explicitly spill it so it can be ----
483 // found by the runtime later. Note: We know all of these spills are ----
484 // independent, but don't bother to exploit that chain wise. DAGCombine ----
485 // will happily do so as needed, so doing it here would be a small compile ----
486 // time win at most. ----
487 SDValue Chain = Builder.getRoot(); 0
488 auto Res = spillIncomingStatepointValue(Incoming, Chain, Builder); 0
489 Ops.push_back(std::get<0>(Res)); 0
490 if (auto *MMO = std::get<2>(Res)) 0
491 MemRefs.push_back(MMO); 0
492 Chain = std::get<1>(Res); 0
493 Builder.DAG.setRoot(Chain); 0
494 } ----
495 ----
496 } ----

498 /// Return true if value V represents the GC value. The behavior is conservative ----
499 /// in case it is not sure that value is not GC the function returns true. ----
500 static bool isGCValue(const Value *V, SelectionDAGBuilder &Builder) { 0
501 auto *Ty = V->getType(); 0
502 if (!Ty->isPtrOrPtrVectorTy()) 0
503 return false; 0
504 if (auto *GFI = Builder.GFI) 0
505 if (auto IsManaged = GFI->getStrategy().isGCManagedPointer(Ty)) 0
506 return *IsManaged; 0
507 return true; // conservative 0
508 } ----
509 ----
510 /// Lower deopt state and gc pointer arguments of the statepoint. The actual ----
511 /// lowering is described in lowerIncomingStatepointValue. This function is ----
512 /// responsible for lowering everything in the right position and playing some ----
513 /// tricks to avoid redundant stack manipulation where possible. On ----
514 /// completion, 'Ops' will contain ready to use operands for machine code ----
515 /// statepoint. The chain nodes will have already been created and the DAG root ----
516 /// will be set to the last value spilled (if any were). ----
517 static void ----
518 lowerStatepointMetaArgs(SmallVectorImpl &Ops, 0
519 SmallVectorImpl &MemRefs, ----
520 SmallVectorImpl &GCPtrs, ----
521 DenseMap &LowerAsVReg, ----
522 SelectionDAGBuilder::StatepointLoweringInfo &SI, ----
523 SelectionDAGBuilder &Builder) { ----
524 // Lower the deopt and gc arguments for this statepoint. Layout will be: ----
525 // deopt argument length, deopt arguments.., gc arguments... ----
526 ----
527 // Figure out what lowering strategy we're going to use for each part ----
528 // Note: Is is conservatively correct to lower both "live-in" and "live-out" ----
529 // as "live-through". A "live-through" variable is one which is "live-in", ----
530 // "live-out", and live throughout the lifetime of the call (i.e. we can find ----
531 // it from any PC within the transitive callee of the statepoint). In ----
532 // particular, if the callee spills callee preserved registers we may not ----
533 // be able to find a value placed in that register during the call. This is ----
534 // fine for live-out, but not for live-through. If we were willing to make ----
535 // assumptions about the code generator producing the callee, we could ----
536 // potentially allow live-through values in callee saved registers. ----
537 const bool LiveInDeopt = 0
538 SI.StatepointFlags & (uint64_t)StatepointFlags::DeoptLiveIn; 0
539 ----
540 // Decide which deriver pointers will go on VRegs ----
541 unsigned MaxVRegPtrs = MaxRegistersForGCPointers.getValue(); 0
542 ----
543 // Pointers used on exceptional path of invoke statepoint. ----
544 // We cannot assing them to VRegs. ----
545 SmallSet LPadPointers; 0
546 if (!UseRegistersForGCPointersInLandingPad) 0
547 if (const auto *StInvoke = 0
548 dyn_cast_or_null(SI.StatepointInstr)) { 0
549 LandingPadInst *LPI = StInvoke->getLandingPadInst(); 0
550 for (const auto *Relocate : SI.GCRelocates) 0
551 if (Relocate->getOperand(0) == LPI) { 0
552 LPadPointers.insert(Builder.getValue(Relocate->getBasePtr())); 0
553 LPadPointers.insert(Builder.getValue(Relocate->getDerivedPtr())); 0
554 } ----
555 } ----
556 ----
557 LLVM_DEBUG(dbgs() << "Deciding how to lower GC Pointers:\n"); 0
558 ----
559 // List of unique lowered GC Pointer values. ----
560 SmallSetVector LoweredGCPtrs; 0
561 // Map lowered GC Pointer value to the index in above vector ----
562 DenseMap GCPtrIndexMap; 0
563 ----
564 unsigned CurNumVRegs = 0; 0
565 ----
566 auto canPassGCPtrOnVReg = [&](SDValue SD) { 0
567 if (SD.getValueType().isVector()) 0
568 return false; 0
569 if (LPadPointers.count(SD)) 0
570 return false; 0
571 return !willLowerDirectly(SD); 0
572 }; 0
573 ----
574 auto processGCPtr = [&](const Value *V) { 0
575 SDValue PtrSD = Builder.getValue(V); 0
576 if (!LoweredGCPtrs.insert(PtrSD)) 0
577 return; // skip duplicates 0
578 GCPtrIndexMap[PtrSD] = LoweredGCPtrs.size() - 1; 0
579 ----
580 assert(!LowerAsVReg.count(PtrSD) && "must not have been seen"); 0
581 if (LowerAsVReg.size() == MaxVRegPtrs) 0
582 return; 0
583 assert(V->getType()->isVectorTy() == PtrSD.getValueType().isVector() && 0
584 "IR and SD types disagree"); ----
585 if (!canPassGCPtrOnVReg(PtrSD)) { 0
586 LLVM_DEBUG(dbgs() << "direct/spill "; PtrSD.dump(&Builder.DAG)); 0
587 return; 0
588 } ----
589 LLVM_DEBUG(dbgs() << "vreg "; PtrSD.dump(&Builder.DAG)); 0
590 LowerAsVReg[PtrSD] = CurNumVRegs++; 0
591 }; 0
592 ----
593 // Process derived pointers first to give them more chance to go on VReg. ----
594 for (const Value *V : SI.Ptrs) 0
595 processGCPtr(V); 0
596 for (const Value *V : SI.Bases) 0
597 processGCPtr(V); 0
598 ----
599 LLVM_DEBUG(dbgs() << LowerAsVReg.size() << " pointers will go in vregs\n"); 0
600 ----
601 auto requireSpillSlot = [&](const Value *V) { 0
602 if (!Builder.DAG.getTargetLoweringInfo().isTypeLegal( 0
603 Builder.getValue(V).getValueType())) 0
604 return true; 0
605 if (isGCValue(V, Builder)) 0
606 return !LowerAsVReg.count(Builder.getValue(V)); 0
607 return !(LiveInDeopt || UseRegistersForDeoptValues); 0
608 }; 0
609 ----
610 // Before we actually start lowering (and allocating spill slots for values), ----
611 // reserve any stack slots which we judge to be profitable to reuse for a ----
612 // particular value. This is purely an optimization over the code below and ----
613 // doesn't change semantics at all. It is important for performance that we ----
614 // reserve slots for both deopt and gc values before lowering either. ----
615 for (const Value *V : SI.DeoptState) { 0
616 if (requireSpillSlot(V)) 0
617 reservePreviousStackSlotForValue(V, Builder); 0
618 } ----
619 ----
620 for (const Value *V : SI.Ptrs) { 0
621 SDValue SDV = Builder.getValue(V); 0
622 if (!LowerAsVReg.count(SDV)) 0
623 reservePreviousStackSlotForValue(V, Builder); 0
624 } ----
625 ----
626 for (const Value *V : SI.Bases) { 0
627 SDValue SDV = Builder.getValue(V); 0
628 if (!LowerAsVReg.count(SDV)) 0
629 reservePreviousStackSlotForValue(V, Builder); 0
630 } ----
631 ----
632 // First, prefix the list with the number of unique values to be ----
633 // lowered. Note that this is the number of *Values* not the ----
634 // number of SDValues required to lower them. ----
635 const int NumVMSArgs = SI.DeoptState.size(); 0
636 pushStackMapConstant(Ops, Builder, NumVMSArgs); 0
637 ----
638 // The vm state arguments are lowered in an opaque manner. We do not know ----
639 // what type of values are contained within. ----
640 LLVM_DEBUG(dbgs() << "Lowering deopt state\n"); 0
641 for (const Value *V : SI.DeoptState) { 0
642 SDValue Incoming; 0
643 // If this is a function argument at a static frame index, generate it as ----
644 // the frame index. ----
645 if (const Argument *Arg = dyn_cast(V)) { 0
646 int FI = Builder.FuncInfo.getArgumentFrameIndex(Arg); 0
647 if (FI != INT_MAX) 0
648 Incoming = Builder.DAG.getFrameIndex(FI, Builder.getFrameIndexTy()); 0
649 } ----
650 if (!Incoming.getNode()) 0
651 Incoming = Builder.getValue(V); 0
652 LLVM_DEBUG(dbgs() << "Value " << *V 0
653 << " requireSpillSlot = " << requireSpillSlot(V) << "\n"); ----
654 lowerIncomingStatepointValue(Incoming, requireSpillSlot(V), Ops, MemRefs, 0
655 Builder); ----
656 } ----
657 ----
658 // Finally, go ahead and lower all the gc arguments. ----
659 pushStackMapConstant(Ops, Builder, LoweredGCPtrs.size()); 0
660 for (SDValue SDV : LoweredGCPtrs) 0
661 lowerIncomingStatepointValue(SDV, !LowerAsVReg.count(SDV), Ops, MemRefs, 0
662 Builder); ----
663 ----
664 // Copy to out vector. LoweredGCPtrs will be empty after this point. ----
665 GCPtrs = LoweredGCPtrs.takeVector(); 0
666 ----
667 // If there are any explicit spill slots passed to the statepoint, record ----
668 // them, but otherwise do not do anything special. These are user provided ----
669 // allocas and give control over placement to the consumer. In this case, ----
670 // it is the contents of the slot which may get updated, not the pointer to ----
671 // the alloca ----
672 SmallVector Allocas; 0
673 for (Value *V : SI.GCArgs) { 0
674 SDValue Incoming = Builder.getValue(V); 0
675 if (FrameIndexSDNode *FI = dyn_cast(Incoming)) { 0
676 // This handles allocas as arguments to the statepoint ----
677 assert(Incoming.getValueType() == Builder.getFrameIndexTy() && 0
678 "Incoming value is a frame index!"); ----
679 Allocas.push_back(Builder.DAG.getTargetFrameIndex( 0
680 FI->getIndex(), Builder.getFrameIndexTy())); ----
681 ----
682 auto &MF = Builder.DAG.getMachineFunction(); 0
683 auto *MMO = getMachineMemOperand(MF, *FI); 0
684 MemRefs.push_back(MMO); 0
685 } ----
686 } ----
687 pushStackMapConstant(Ops, Builder, Allocas.size()); 0
688 Ops.append(Allocas.begin(), Allocas.end()); 0
689 ----
690 // Now construct GC base/derived map; ----
691 pushStackMapConstant(Ops, Builder, SI.Ptrs.size()); 0
692 SDLoc L = Builder.getCurSDLoc(); 0
693 for (unsigned i = 0; i < SI.Ptrs.size(); ++i) { 0
694 SDValue Base = Builder.getValue(SI.Bases[i]); 0
695 assert(GCPtrIndexMap.count(Base) && "base not found in index map"); 0
696 Ops.push_back( 0
697 Builder.DAG.getTargetConstant(GCPtrIndexMap[Base], L, MVT::i64)); 0
698 SDValue Derived = Builder.getValue(SI.Ptrs[i]); 0
699 assert(GCPtrIndexMap.count(Derived) && "derived not found in index map"); 0
700 Ops.push_back( 0
701 Builder.DAG.getTargetConstant(GCPtrIndexMap[Derived], L, MVT::i64)); 0
702 } ----
703 } 0
704 ----
705 SDValue SelectionDAGBuilder::LowerAsSTATEPOINT( 0
706 SelectionDAGBuilder::StatepointLoweringInfo &SI) { ----
707 // The basic scheme here is that information about both the original call and ----
708 // the safepoint is encoded in the CallInst. We create a temporary call and ----
709 // lower it, then reverse engineer the calling sequence. ----
710 ----
711 NumOfStatepoints++; 0
712 // Clear state ----
713 StatepointLowering.startNewStatepoint(*this); 0
714 assert(SI.Bases.size() == SI.Ptrs.size() && "Pointer without base!"); 0
715 assert((GFI || SI.Bases.empty()) && 0
716 "No gc specified, so cannot relocate pointers!"); ----
717 ----
718 LLVM_DEBUG(dbgs() << "Lowering statepoint " << *SI.StatepointInstr << "\n"); 0
719 #ifndef NDEBUG ----
720 for (const auto *Reloc : SI.GCRelocates) 0
721 if (Reloc->getParent() == SI.StatepointInstr->getParent()) 0
722 StatepointLowering.scheduleRelocCall(*Reloc); 0
723 #endif ----
724 ----
725 // Lower statepoint vmstate and gcstate arguments ----
726 ----
727 // All lowered meta args. ----
728 SmallVector LoweredMetaArgs; 0
729 // Lowered GC pointers (subset of above). ----
730 SmallVector LoweredGCArgs; 0
731 SmallVector MemRefs; 0
732 // Maps derived pointer SDValue to statepoint result of relocated pointer. ----
733 DenseMap LowerAsVReg; 0
734 lowerStatepointMetaArgs(LoweredMetaArgs, MemRefs, LoweredGCArgs, LowerAsVReg, 0
735 SI, *this); ----
736 ----
737 // Now that we've emitted the spills, we need to update the root so that the ----
738 // call sequence is ordered correctly. ----
739 SI.CLI.setChain(getRoot()); 0
740 ----
741 // Get call node, we will replace it later with statepoint ----
742 SDValue ReturnVal; 0
743 SDNode *CallNode; ----
744 std::tie(ReturnVal, CallNode) = lowerCallFromStatepointLoweringInfo(SI, *this); 0
745 ----
746 // Construct the actual GC_TRANSITION_START, STATEPOINT, and GC_TRANSITION_END ----
747 // nodes with all the appropriate arguments and return values. ----
748 ----
749 // Call Node: Chain, Target, {Args}, RegMask, [Glue] ----
750 SDValue Chain = CallNode->getOperand(0); 0
751 ----
752 SDValue Glue; 0
753 bool CallHasIncomingGlue = CallNode->getGluedNode(); 0
754 if (CallHasIncomingGlue) { 0
755 // Glue is always last operand ----
756 Glue = CallNode->getOperand(CallNode->getNumOperands() - 1); 0
757 } ----
758 ----
759 // Build the GC_TRANSITION_START node if necessary. ----
760 // ----
761 // The operands to the GC_TRANSITION_{START,END} nodes are laid out in the ----
762 // order in which they appear in the call to the statepoint intrinsic. If ----
763 // any of the operands is a pointer-typed, that operand is immediately ----
764 // followed by a SRCVALUE for the pointer that may be used during lowering ----
765 // (e.g. to form MachinePointerInfo values for loads/stores). ----
766 const bool IsGCTransition = 0
767 (SI.StatepointFlags & (uint64_t)StatepointFlags::GCTransition) == 0
768 (uint64_t)StatepointFlags::GCTransition; ----
769 if (IsGCTransition) { 0
770 SmallVector TSOps; 0
771 ----
772 // Add chain ----
773 TSOps.push_back(Chain); 0
774 ----
775 // Add GC transition arguments ----
776 for (const Value *V : SI.GCTransitionArgs) { 0
777 TSOps.push_back(getValue(V)); 0
778 if (V->getType()->isPointerTy()) 0
779 TSOps.push_back(DAG.getSrcValue(V)); 0
780 } ----
781 ----
782 // Add glue if necessary ----
783 if (CallHasIncomingGlue) 0
784 TSOps.push_back(Glue); 0
785 ----
786 SDVTList NodeTys = DAG.getVTList(MVT::Other, MVT::Glue); 0
787 ----
788 SDValue GCTransitionStart = ----
789 DAG.getNode(ISD::GC_TRANSITION_START, getCurSDLoc(), NodeTys, TSOps); 0
790 ----
791 Chain = GCTransitionStart.getValue(0); 0
792 Glue = GCTransitionStart.getValue(1); 0
793 } 0
794 ----
795 // TODO: Currently, all of these operands are being marked as read/write in ----
796 // PrologEpilougeInserter.cpp, we should special case the VMState arguments ----
797 // and flags to be read-only. ----
798 SmallVector Ops; 0
799 ----
800 // Add the and constants. ----
801 Ops.push_back(DAG.getTargetConstant(SI.ID, getCurSDLoc(), MVT::i64)); 0
802 Ops.push_back( 0
803 DAG.getTargetConstant(SI.NumPatchBytes, getCurSDLoc(), MVT::i32)); 0
804 ----
805 // Calculate and push starting position of vmstate arguments ----
806 // Get number of arguments incoming directly into call node ----
807 unsigned NumCallRegArgs = ----
808 CallNode->getNumOperands() - (CallHasIncomingGlue ? 4 : 3); 0
809 Ops.push_back(DAG.getTargetConstant(NumCallRegArgs, getCurSDLoc(), MVT::i32)); 0
810 ----
811 // Add call target ----
812 SDValue CallTarget = SDValue(CallNode->getOperand(1).getNode(), 0); 0
813 Ops.push_back(CallTarget); 0
814 ----
815 // Add call arguments ----
816 // Get position of register mask in the call ----
817 SDNode::op_iterator RegMaskIt; ----
818 if (CallHasIncomingGlue) 0
819 RegMaskIt = CallNode->op_end() - 2; 0
820 else ----
821 RegMaskIt = CallNode->op_end() - 1; 0
822 Ops.insert(Ops.end(), CallNode->op_begin() + 2, RegMaskIt); 0
823 ----
824 // Add a constant argument for the calling convention ----
825 pushStackMapConstant(Ops, *this, SI.CLI.CallConv); 0
826 ----
827 // Add a constant argument for the flags ----
828 uint64_t Flags = SI.StatepointFlags; 0
829 assert(((Flags & ~(uint64_t)StatepointFlags::MaskAll) == 0) && 0
830 "Unknown flag used"); ----
831 pushStackMapConstant(Ops, *this, Flags); 0
832 ----
833 // Insert all vmstate and gcstate arguments ----
834 llvm::append_range(Ops, LoweredMetaArgs); 0
835 ----
836 // Add register mask from call node ----
837 Ops.push_back(*RegMaskIt); 0
838 ----
839 // Add chain ----
840 Ops.push_back(Chain); 0
841 ----
842 // Same for the glue, but we add it only if original call had it ----
843 if (Glue.getNode()) 0
844 Ops.push_back(Glue); 0
845 ----
846 // Compute return values. Provide a glue output since we consume one as ----
847 // input. This allows someone else to chain off us as needed. ----
848 SmallVector NodeTys; 0
849 for (auto SD : LoweredGCArgs) { 0
850 if (!LowerAsVReg.count(SD)) 0
851 continue; 0
852 NodeTys.push_back(SD.getValueType()); 0
853 } ----
854 LLVM_DEBUG(dbgs() << "Statepoint has " << NodeTys.size() << " results\n"); 0
855 assert(NodeTys.size() == LowerAsVReg.size() && "Inconsistent GC Ptr lowering"); 0
856 NodeTys.push_back(MVT::Other); 0
857 NodeTys.push_back(MVT::Glue); 0
858 ----
859 unsigned NumResults = NodeTys.size(); 0
860 MachineSDNode *StatepointMCNode = ----
861 DAG.getMachineNode(TargetOpcode::STATEPOINT, getCurSDLoc(), NodeTys, Ops); 0
862 DAG.setNodeMemRefs(StatepointMCNode, MemRefs); 0
863 ----
864 // For values lowered to tied-defs, create the virtual registers if used ----
865 // in other blocks. For local gc.relocate record appropriate statepoint ----
866 // result in StatepointLoweringState. ----
867 DenseMap VirtRegs; 0
868 for (const auto *Relocate : SI.GCRelocates) { 0
869 Value *Derived = Relocate->getDerivedPtr(); 0
870 SDValue SD = getValue(Derived); 0
871 if (!LowerAsVReg.count(SD)) 0
872 continue; 0
873 ----
874 SDValue Relocated = SDValue(StatepointMCNode, LowerAsVReg[SD]); 0
875 ----
876 // Handle local relocate. Note that different relocates might ----
877 // map to the same SDValue. ----
878 if (SI.StatepointInstr->getParent() == Relocate->getParent()) { 0
879 SDValue Res = StatepointLowering.getLocation(SD); 0
880 if (Res) 0
881 assert(Res == Relocated); 0
882 else ----
883 StatepointLowering.setLocation(SD, Relocated); 0
884 continue; 0
885 } 0
886 ----
887 // Handle multiple gc.relocates of the same input efficiently. ----
888 if (VirtRegs.count(SD)) 0
889 continue; 0
890 ----
891 auto *RetTy = Relocate->getType(); 0
892 Register Reg = FuncInfo.CreateRegs(RetTy); 0
893 RegsForValue RFV(*DAG.getContext(), DAG.getTargetLoweringInfo(), 0
894 DAG.getDataLayout(), Reg, RetTy, std::nullopt); 0
895 SDValue Chain = DAG.getRoot(); 0
896 RFV.getCopyToRegs(Relocated, DAG, getCurSDLoc(), Chain, nullptr); 0
897 PendingExports.push_back(Chain); 0
898 ----
899 VirtRegs[SD] = Reg; 0
900 } 0
901 ----
902 // Record for later use how each relocation was lowered. This is needed to ----
903 // allow later gc.relocates to mirror the lowering chosen. ----
904 const Instruction *StatepointInstr = SI.StatepointInstr; 0
905 auto &RelocationMap = FuncInfo.StatepointRelocationMaps[StatepointInstr]; 0
906 for (const GCRelocateInst *Relocate : SI.GCRelocates) { 0
907 const Value *V = Relocate->getDerivedPtr(); 0
908 SDValue SDV = getValue(V); 0
909 SDValue Loc = StatepointLowering.getLocation(SDV); 0
910 ----
911 bool IsLocal = (Relocate->getParent() == StatepointInstr->getParent()); 0
912 ----
913 RecordType Record; 0
914 if (IsLocal && LowerAsVReg.count(SDV)) { 0
915 // Result is already stored in StatepointLowering ----
916 Record.type = RecordType::SDValueNode; 0
917 } else if (LowerAsVReg.count(SDV)) { 0
918 Record.type = RecordType::VReg; 0
919 assert(VirtRegs.count(SDV)); 0
920 Record.payload.Reg = VirtRegs[SDV]; 0
921 } else if (Loc.getNode()) { 0
922 Record.type = RecordType::Spill; 0
923 Record.payload.FI = cast(Loc)->getIndex(); 0
924 } else { ----
925 Record.type = RecordType::NoRelocate; 0
926 // If we didn't relocate a value, we'll essentialy end up inserting an ----
927 // additional use of the original value when lowering the gc.relocate. ----
928 // We need to make sure the value is available at the new use, which ----
929 // might be in another block. ----
930 if (Relocate->getParent() != StatepointInstr->getParent()) 0
931 ExportFromCurrentBlock(V); 0
932 } ----
933 RelocationMap[Relocate] = Record; 0
934 } ----
935 ----
936 ----
937 ----
938 SDNode *SinkNode = StatepointMCNode; 0
939 ----
940 // Build the GC_TRANSITION_END node if necessary. ----
941 // ----
942 // See the comment above regarding GC_TRANSITION_START for the layout of ----
943 // the operands to the GC_TRANSITION_END node. ----
944 if (IsGCTransition) { 0
945 SmallVector TEOps; 0
946 ----
947 // Add chain ----
948 TEOps.push_back(SDValue(StatepointMCNode, NumResults - 2)); 0
949 ----
950 // Add GC transition arguments ----
951 for (const Value *V : SI.GCTransitionArgs) { 0
952 TEOps.push_back(getValue(V)); 0
953 if (V->getType()->isPointerTy()) 0
954 TEOps.push_back(DAG.getSrcValue(V)); 0
955 } ----
956 ----
957 // Add glue ----
958 TEOps.push_back(SDValue(StatepointMCNode, NumResults - 1)); 0
959 ----
960 SDVTList NodeTys = DAG.getVTList(MVT::Other, MVT::Glue); 0
961 ----
962 SDValue GCTransitionStart = ----
963 DAG.getNode(ISD::GC_TRANSITION_END, getCurSDLoc(), NodeTys, TEOps); 0
964 ----
965 SinkNode = GCTransitionStart.getNode(); 0
966 } 0
967 ----
968 // Replace original call ----
969 // Call: ch,glue = CALL ... ----
970 // Statepoint: [gc relocates],ch,glue = STATEPOINT ... ----
971 unsigned NumSinkValues = SinkNode->getNumValues(); 0
972 SDValue StatepointValues[2] = {SDValue(SinkNode, NumSinkValues - 2), ----
973 SDValue(SinkNode, NumSinkValues - 1)}; 0
974 DAG.ReplaceAllUsesWith(CallNode, StatepointValues); 0
975 // Remove original call node ----
976 DAG.DeleteNode(CallNode); 0
977 ----
978 // Since we always emit CopyToRegs (even for local relocates), we must ----
979 // update root, so that they are emitted before any local uses. ----
980 (void)getControlRoot(); 0
981 ----
982 // TODO: A better future implementation would be to emit a single variable ----
983 // argument, variable return value STATEPOINT node here and then hookup the ----
984 // return value of each gc.relocate to the respective output of the ----
985 // previously emitted STATEPOINT value. Unfortunately, this doesn't appear ----
986 // to actually be possible today. ----
987 ----
988 return ReturnVal; 0
989 } 0
990 ----
991 /// Return two gc.results if present. First result is a block local ----
992 /// gc.result, second result is a non-block local gc.result. Corresponding ----
993 /// entry will be nullptr if not present. ----
994 static std::pair ----
995 getGCResultLocality(const GCStatepointInst &S) { 0
996 std::pair Res(nullptr, nullptr); 0
997 for (const auto *U : S.users()) { 0
998 auto *GRI = dyn_cast(U); 0
999 if (!GRI) 0
1000 continue; 0
1001 if (GRI->getParent() == S.getParent()) 0
1002 Res.first = GRI; 0
1003 else ----
1004 Res.second = GRI; 0
1005 } ----
1006 return Res; 0
1007 } ----
1008 ----
1009 void ----
1010 SelectionDAGBuilder::LowerStatepoint(const GCStatepointInst &I, 0
1011 const BasicBlock *EHPadBB /*= nullptr*/) { ----
1012 assert(I.getCallingConv() != CallingConv::AnyReg && 0
1013 "anyregcc is not supported on statepoints!"); ----
1014 ----
1015 #ifndef NDEBUG ----
1016 // Check that the associated GCStrategy expects to encounter statepoints. ----
1017 assert(GFI->getStrategy().useStatepoints() && 0
1018 "GCStrategy does not expect to encounter statepoints"); ----
1019 #endif ----
1020 ----
1021 SDValue ActualCallee; 0
1022 SDValue Callee = getValue(I.getActualCalledOperand()); 0
1023 ----
1024 if (I.getNumPatchBytes() > 0) { 0
1025 // If we've been asked to emit a nop sequence instead of a call instruction ----
1026 // for this statepoint then don't lower the call target, but use a constant ----
1027 // `undef` instead. Not lowering the call target lets statepoint clients ----
1028 // get away without providing a physical address for the symbolic call ----
1029 // target at link time. ----
1030 ActualCallee = DAG.getUNDEF(Callee.getValueType()); 0
1031 } else { ----
1032 ActualCallee = Callee; 0
1033 } ----
1034 ----
1035 StatepointLoweringInfo SI(DAG); 0
1036 populateCallLoweringInfo(SI.CLI, &I, GCStatepointInst::CallArgsBeginPos, 0
1037 I.getNumCallArgs(), ActualCallee, 0
1038 I.getActualReturnType(), false /* IsPatchPoint */); ----
1039 ----
1040 // There may be duplication in the gc.relocate list; such as two copies of ----
1041 // each relocation on normal and exceptional path for an invoke. We only ----
1042 // need to spill once and record one copy in the stackmap, but we need to ----
1043 // reload once per gc.relocate. (Dedupping gc.relocates is trickier and best ----
1044 // handled as a CSE problem elsewhere.) ----
1045 // TODO: There a couple of major stackmap size optimizations we could do ----
1046 // here if we wished. ----
1047 // 1) If we've encountered a derived pair {B, D}, we don't need to actually ----
1048 // record {B,B} if it's seen later. ----
1049 // 2) Due to rematerialization, actual derived pointers are somewhat rare; ----
1050 // given that, we could change the format to record base pointer relocations ----
1051 // separately with half the space. This would require a format rev and a ----
1052 // fairly major rework of the STATEPOINT node though. ----
1053 SmallSet Seen; 0
1054 for (const GCRelocateInst *Relocate : I.getGCRelocates()) { 0
1055 SI.GCRelocates.push_back(Relocate); 0
1056 ----
1057 SDValue DerivedSD = getValue(Relocate->getDerivedPtr()); 0
1058 if (Seen.insert(DerivedSD).second) { 0
1059 SI.Bases.push_back(Relocate->getBasePtr()); 0
1060 SI.Ptrs.push_back(Relocate->getDerivedPtr()); 0
1061 } ----
1062 } 0
1063 ----
1064 // If we find a deopt value which isn't explicitly added, we need to ----
1065 // ensure it gets lowered such that gc cycles occurring before the ----
1066 // deoptimization event during the lifetime of the call don't invalidate ----
1067 // the pointer we're deopting with. Note that we assume that all ----
1068 // pointers passed to deopt are base pointers; relaxing that assumption ----
1069 // would require relatively large changes to how we represent relocations. ----
1070 for (Value *V : I.deopt_operands()) { 0
1071 if (!isGCValue(V, *this)) 0
1072 continue; 0
1073 if (Seen.insert(getValue(V)).second) { 0
1074 SI.Bases.push_back(V); 0
1075 SI.Ptrs.push_back(V); 0
1076 } ----
1077 } ----
1078 ----
1079 SI.GCArgs = ArrayRef(I.gc_args_begin(), I.gc_args_end()); 0
1080 SI.StatepointInstr = &I; 0
1081 SI.ID = I.getID(); 0
1082 ----
1083 SI.DeoptState = ArrayRef(I.deopt_begin(), I.deopt_end()); 0
1084 SI.GCTransitionArgs = ArrayRef(I.gc_transition_args_begin(), 0
1085 I.gc_transition_args_end()); ----
1086 ----
1087 SI.StatepointFlags = I.getFlags(); 0
1088 SI.NumPatchBytes = I.getNumPatchBytes(); 0
1089 SI.EHPadBB = EHPadBB; 0
1090 ----
1091 SDValue ReturnValue = LowerAsSTATEPOINT(SI); 0
1092 ----
1093 // Export the result value if needed ----
1094 const auto GCResultLocality = getGCResultLocality(I); 0
1095 ----
1096 if (!GCResultLocality.first && !GCResultLocality.second) { 0
1097 // The return value is not needed, just generate a poison value. ----
1098 // Note: This covers the void return case. ----
1099 setValue(&I, DAG.getIntPtrConstant(-1, getCurSDLoc())); 0
1100 return; 0
1101 } ----
1102 ----
1103 if (GCResultLocality.first) { 0
1104 // Result value will be used in a same basic block. Don't export it or ----
1105 // perform any explicit register copies. The gc_result will simply grab ----
1106 // this value. ----
1107 setValue(&I, ReturnValue); 0
1108 } ----
1109 ----
1110 if (!GCResultLocality.second) 0
1111 return; 0
1112 // Result value will be used in a different basic block so we need to export ----
1113 // it now. Default exporting mechanism will not work here because statepoint ----
1114 // call has a different type than the actual call. It means that by default ----
1115 // llvm will create export register of the wrong type (always i32 in our ----
1116 // case). So instead we need to create export register with correct type ----
1117 // manually. ----
1118 // TODO: To eliminate this problem we can remove gc.result intrinsics ----
1119 // completely and make statepoint call to return a tuple. ----
1120 Type *RetTy = GCResultLocality.second->getType(); 0
1121 Register Reg = FuncInfo.CreateRegs(RetTy); 0
1122 RegsForValue RFV(*DAG.getContext(), DAG.getTargetLoweringInfo(), 0
1123 DAG.getDataLayout(), Reg, RetTy, 0
1124 I.getCallingConv()); 0
1125 SDValue Chain = DAG.getEntryNode(); 0
1126 ----
1127 RFV.getCopyToRegs(ReturnValue, DAG, getCurSDLoc(), Chain, nullptr); 0
